# Grafana Legacy Alerting to Unified Alerting Migration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement both the legacy alerting engine and the unified alerting (ngalert) engine: the legacy alert rule storage, the unified alert rule storage, and the migration script that converts legacy rules to unified format.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

    18→func UidToName(uid string) (string, error) {
    19→	data, err := base64.RawURLEncoding.DecodeString(uid)
    20→	if err != nil {
    21→		return uid, err
    22→	}
    23→	return string(data), nil
    24→}
    25→
    26→func IntegrationToPostableGrafanaReceiver(integration *models.Integration) (*apimodels.PostableGrafanaReceiver, error) {
    27→	postable := &apimodels.PostableGrafanaReceiver{
    28→		UID:                   integration.UID,
    29→		Name:                  integration.Name,
    30→		Type:                  string(integration.Config.Type()),
    31→		DisableResolveMessage: integration.DisableResolveMessage,
    32→		SecureSettings:        maps.Clone(integration.SecureSettings),
    33→	}
    34→
    35→	// Alertmanager will fail validation with nil Settings , so ensure we always have at least an empty map.
    36→	settings := integration.Settings
    37→	if settings == nil {
    38→		settings = make(map[string]any)
    39→	}
    40→
    41→	jsonBytes, err := json.Marshal(settings)
    42→	if err != nil {
    43→		return nil, err
    44→	}
    45→	postable.Settings = jsonBytes
    46→	return postable, nil
    47→}

    31→// StateToPostableAlert converts a state to a model that is accepted by Alertmanager. Annotations and Labels are copied from the state.
    32→// - if state has at least one result, a new label '__value_string__' is added to the label set
    33→// - the alert's GeneratorURL is constructed to point to the alert detail view

     1→# Next generation alerting (ngalert) in Grafana 8
     2→
     3→Ngalert (Next generation alert) is the next generation of alerting in Grafana 8.
     4→
     5→## Overview
     6→
     7→The ngalert package can be found in `pkg/services/ngalert` and has the following sub-packages:
     8→
     9→    - api
    10→    - eval
    11→    - logging
    12→    - metrics
    13→    - models
    14→    - notifier
    15→    - schedule
    16→    - sender
    17→    - state
    18→    - store
    19→    - tests
    20→
    21→## Scheduling and evaluation of alert rules
    22→
    23→The scheduling of alert rules happens in the `schedule` package. This package is responsible for managing the evaluation
    24→of alert rules including checking for new alert rules and stopping the evaluation of deleted alert rules.
    25→
    26→The scheduler runs at a fixed interval, called its heartbeat, in which it does a number of tasks:
    27→
    28→1. Fetch the alert rules for all organizations (excluding disabled)
    29→2. Start a goroutine (if this is a new alert rule or the scheduler has just started) to evaluate the alert rule
    30→3. Send an `*evaluation` event to the goroutine for each alert rule if its interval has elapsed
    31→4. Stop the goroutines for all alert rules that have been deleted since the last heartbeat
    32→
    33→The function that evaluates each alert rule is called `run`. It waits for an `*evaluation` event (sent each
    34→interval seconds elapsed and is configurable per alert rule) and then evaluates the alert rule. To ensure that the
    35→scheduler is evaluating the latest version of the alert rule it compares its local version of the alert rule with that
    36→in the `*evaluation` event, fetching the latest version of the alert rule from the
... (truncated)

    18→func UidToName(uid string) (string, error) {
    19→	data, err := base64.RawURLEncoding.DecodeString(uid)
    20→	if err != nil {
    21→		return uid, err
    22→	}
    23→	return string(data), nil
    24→}
    25→
    26→func IntegrationToPostableGrafanaReceiver(integration *models.Integration) (*apimodels.PostableGrafanaReceiver, error) {
    27→	postable := &apimodels.PostableGrafanaReceiver{
    28→		UID:                   integration.UID,
    29→		Name:                  integration.Name,
    30→		Type:                  string(integration.Config.Type()),
    31→		DisableResolveMessage: integration.DisableResolveMessage,
    32→		SecureSettings:        maps.Clone(integration.SecureSettings),
    33→	}
    34→
    35→	// Alertmanager will fail validation with nil Settings , so ensure we always have at least an empty map.
    36→	settings := integration.Settings
    37→	if settings == nil {
    38→		settings = make(map[string]any)
    39→	}
    40→
    41→	jsonBytes, err := json.Marshal(settings)
    42→	if err != nil {
    43→		return nil, err
    44→	}
    45→	postable.Settings = jsonBytes
    46→	return postable, nil
    47→}

    23→// CreateOrgMigratedKVStoreEntries creates kv store entries for each organization if the migration has been run.
    24→// This is needed now that we've changed the semantics of data loss when upgrading / rolling back. If a user who previously
    25→// upgraded were to rollback and upgrade again without clean_upgrade, then since they don't have org-level migrated states
    26→// it will attempt to upgrade their orgs as if they had never upgraded before. This will almost definitely fail with
    27→// duplicate key errors.
    28→//
    29→// In addition, this changes the entry for orgId=0 to be better named as it no longer tracks whether the
    30→// migration has been run, but rather the current alerting type of Grafana; Legacy or UnifiedAlerting. This is used to
    31→// detect transitions between Legacy and UnifiedAlerting by comparing to the desired type in the configuration.

"     1\u2192# Next generation alerting (ngalert) in Grafana 8\n     2\u2192\n     3\u2192Ngalert (Next generation alert) is the next generation of alerting in Grafana 8.\n     4\u2192\n     5\u2192## Overview\n     6\u2192\n     7\u2192The ngalert package can be found in `pkg/services/ngalert` and has the following sub-packages:\n     8\u2192\n     9\u2192    - api\n    10\u2192    - eval\n    11\u2192    - logging\n    12\u2192    - metrics\n    13\u2192    - models\n    14\u2192    - notifier\n    15\u2192    - schedule\n    16\u2192    - sender\n    17\u2192    - state\n    18\u2192    - store\n    19\u2192    - tests\n    20\u2192\n    21\u2192## Scheduling and evaluation of alert rules\n    22\u2192\n    23\u2192The scheduling of alert rules happens in the `schedule` package. This package is responsible for managing the evaluation\n    24\u2192of alert rules including checking for new alert rules and stopping the evaluation of deleted alert rules.\n    25\u2192\n    26\u2192The scheduler runs at a fixed interval, called its heartbeat, in which it does a number of tasks:\n    27\u2192\n    28\u21921. Fetch the alert rules for all organizations (excluding disabled)\n    29\u21922. Start a goroutine (if this is a new alert rule or the scheduler has just started) to evaluate the alert rule\n    30\u21923. Send an `*evaluation` event to the goroutine for each alert rule if its interval has elapsed\n    31\u21924. Stop the goroutines for all alert rules that have been deleted since the last heartbeat\n    32\u2192\n    33\u2192The function that evaluates each alert rule is called `run`. It waits for an `*evaluation` event (sent each\n    34\u2192interval seconds elapsed and is configurable per alert rule) and then evaluates the alert rule. To ensure that the\n    35\u2192scheduler is evaluating the latest version of the alert rule it compares its local version of the alert rule with that\n    36\u2192in the `*evaluation` event, fetching the latest version of the alert rule from the database if the version numbers\n    37\u2192mismatch. It then invokes the Evaluator which evaluates any queries, classic conditions or expressions in alert rule\n    38\u2192and passes the results of this evaluation to the State Manager. An evaluation can return no results in the case of\n    39\u2192NoData or Error, a single result in the case of classic conditions, or more than one result if the alert rule is\n    40\u2192multi-dimensional (i.e. one result per label set). In the case of multi-dimensional alert rules the results from an\n    41\u2192evaluation should never contain more than one per label set.\n    42\u2192\n    43\u2192The State Manager is responsible for determining the current state of the alert rule (normal, pending, firing, etc) by\n    44\u2192comparing each evaluation result to the previous evaluations of the same label set in the state cache. Given a label set,\n    45\u2192it updates the state cache with the new current state, the evaluation time of the current evaluation and appends the\n    46\u2192current evaluation to the slice of previous evaluations. If the alert changes state (i.e. pending to firing)\n    47\u2192then it also creates an annotation to mark it on the dashboard and panel for this alert rule.\n    48\u2192\n    49\u2192You might have noticed that so far we have avoided using the word \"Alert\" and instead talked about evaluation results\n    50\u2192and the current state of an alert rule. The reason for that is at this time in the evaluation of an alert rule the\n    51\u2192State Manager does not know about alerts, it just knows for each label set the state of an alert rule, the current\n    52\u2192evaluation and previous evaluations.\n    53\u2192\n    54\u2192## Notification of alerts\n    55\u2192\n    56\u2192When an evaluation transitions the state of an alert rule for a given label set from pending to firing or from firing\n    57\u2192to normal the scheduler creates an alert instance and passes it to Alertmanager. In the case where a label set is\n    58\u2192transitioning from pending to firing the state of the alert instance is \"Firing\" and when transitioning from firing to\n    59\u2192normal the state of the alert instance is \"Normal\".\n    60\u2192\n    61\u2192### Which Alertmanager?\n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192In ngalert it is possible to send alerts to the internal Alertmanager, an external Alertmanager, or both.\n    64\u2192\n    65\u2192The internal Alertmanager is called `MultiOrgAlertmanager` and creates an Alertmanager for each organization in\n    66\u2192Grafana to preserve isolation between organizations in Grafana. The `MultiOrgAlertmanager` receives alerts from the\n    67\u2192scheduler and then forwards the alert to the correct Alertmanager for the organization.\n    68\u2192\n    69\u2192When Grafana is configured to send alerts to an external Alertmanager it does so via the sender which creates an\n    70\u2192abstraction over notification of alerts and discovery of external Alertmanagers in Prometheus. The sender receives\n    71\u2192alerts via the `SendAlerts` function and then passes them to Prometheus.\n    72\u2192\n    73\u2192### How does Alertmanager turn alerts into notifications?\n    74\u2192\n    75\u2192Alertmanager receives alerts via the `PutAlerts` function. Each alert is validated and its annotations and labels are\n    76\u2192normalized, then the alerts are put in an in-memory structure. The dispatcher iterates over the alerts and matches\n    77\u2192it to a route in the configuration as explained [here](https://prometheus.io/docs/alerting/latest/configuration/#route).\n    78\u2192\n    79\u2192The alert is then matched to an alert group depending on the configuration in the route. The alert is then sent through\n    80\u2192a number of stages including silencing and inhibition (which is currently not supported) and at last the receiver which can include wait, de-duplication,\n    81\u2192retry.\n    82\u2192\n    83\u2192### What are notification channels?\n    84\u2192\n    85\u2192Notification channels receive alerts and turn them into notifications and is often the last callback in the receiver\n    86\u2192after wait, de-duplication and retry.\n    87\u2192\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"

tracking.\\n\\nThe complete migration flow transitions dashboards alerts (stored in the legacy `alert` table) with their notification channels to Grafana's unified alerting system, mapping legacy Migration\\n\\nThe migration from Grafana's legacy alerting system to the unified alerting (ngalert) engine is implemented across multiple coordinated components in the grafana/grafana repository.\\n\\n### Legacy Alert Schema Definition\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/alert_mig.go** defines the legacy alerting database schema with tables:\\n- `alert` table: Core legacy alert records with fields like dashboard_id, panel_id, name, message, settings, frequency, severity, state, and handler\\n- `alert_notification` table: Legacy notification channels (email, Slack, etc.)\\n- `alert_rule_tag` table: Tags associated with legacy alerts\\n- `alert_notification_state` table: Notification delivery state tracking\\n\\n### Unified Alert Rule Storage\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/tables.go** defines the unified alerting schema:\\n- `alert_rule` table: New alert rule format with condition, data (queries), interval, labels, annotations, rule group organization\\n- `alert_rule_version` table: Audit trail and versioning of alert rule changes\\n- `alert_configuration` table: Alertmanager configuration per organization\\n\\n**pkg/services/ngalert/store/alert_rule.go** implements the unified alert rule storage service providing database access and CRUD operations for alert rules.\\n\\n### Migration Scripts\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/ualert.go** is the primary migration orchestrator containing:\\n- `FixEarlyMigration()`: Fixes unified alerting configurations created before version 8.2 (org_id=0 issue)\\n- `AddDashboardUIDPanelIDMigration()`: Extracts dashboard_uid and panel_id from `__dashboardUid__` and `__panelId__` annotations\\n- `upgradeNgAlerting struct`: Handles alertmanager file relocations during migration\\n\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/migration_service_migration.go** manages migration status tracking by moving legacy alert migration completion status from the migration_log table to kvstore with namespace `ngalert.migration` and key `migrated`.\\n\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/org_upgrade_state_mig.go** creates per-organization migration state entries tracking whether each org is in \\\"Legacy\\\" or \\\"UnifiedAlerting\\\" mode.\\n\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/created_folders_mig.go** migrates the record of folders created during migration (dashboards with created_by=-8) to kvstore.\\n\\nSupporting schema migrations handle:\\n- **alert_rule_version_guid_mig.go**: GUID migration for alert rule versions\\n- **rule_creator_mig.go**: Tracks rule creator and updater metadata\\n- **rule_group_index_migration.go**: Manages alert rule group ordering\\n- **recording_rules_mig.go**: Adds recording rule support columns\\n- **alert_rule_keep_firing_for.go**: Adds keep_firing_for duration support\\n- **alert_rule_missing_series_evals_to_resolve.go**: Adds missing series resolution handling\\n- **receiver_scope_mig.go**: Manages receiver action scopes for access control\\n\\n### Field Mapping and Compatibility\\n**pkg/services/ngalert/models/alert_rule.go** defines migration-related labels and annotations that map legacy alert fields:\\n- `MigratedLabelPrefix = \\\"__legacy_\\\"`: Marks migrated alerts\\n- `MigratedContactLabelPrefix`: Routes migrated alerts to specific migrated notification channels\\n- `MigratedAlertIdAnnotation = \\\"__alertId__\\\"`: Stores the ID of the original legacy alert\\n- `MigratedMessageAnnotation`: Maps legacy alert message field\\n\\n**pkg/services/ngalert/store/compat.go** provides conversion functions:\\n- `alertRuleToModelsAlertRule()`: Converts database record to AlertRule model\\n- `alertRuleFromModelsAlertRule()`: Converts AlertRule model to database record\\n\\n**pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/legacy_storage/compat.go** handles legacy notification channel conversion:\\n- `IntegrationToPostableGrafanaReceiver()`: Converts legacy integration to receiver format\\n- `PostableApiReceiverToReceiver()`: Converts API receiver to internal model\\n- `PostableGrafanaReceiverToIntegration()`: Reverse conversion for integration\\n\\n**pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/legacy_storage/** directory provides compatibility layer:\\n- `config.go`: Legacy configuration management\\n- `receivers.go`: Legacy receiver/notification channel handling\\n\\n### Migration Orchestration\\n**pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/migrations.go** is the central migration registry that orchestrates all migrations in the correct sequence, ensuring legacy alert tables are created first, then migrated to unified alerting schema, with proper state tracking.\\n\\nThe complete migration flow transitions dashboards alerts (stored in the legacy `alert` table) with their notification channels to Grafana's unified alerting system, mapping legacy fields to the new alert rule structure while maintaining audit trails and migration state across all organizations.\"\n}\n",
